<h1 class="firstHeading" id="firstHeading" lang="en">David Hasselhoff</h1>
<div class="mw-body-content" id="bodyContent">
<div id="siteSub">From Wikipedia, the free encyclopedia</div>
<div id="contentSub"><div class="flaggedrevs_short flaggedrevs_stable_synced plainlinks noprint nomobile" id="mw-fr-revisiontag"><div class="flaggedrevs_short_basic"><img alt="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page." class="flaggedrevs-icon" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/doc-magnify.png" title="Changes must be reviewed before being displayed on this page."/><img alt="show/hide details" class="fr-toggle-arrow" id="mw-fr-revisiontoggle" src="/w/extensions/FlaggedRevs/frontend/modules/img/arrow-down.png" style="display:none;"/></div>

<p><b>David Michael Hasselhoff</b> (born July 17, 1952),<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-filmref_1-0"><a href="#cite_note-filmref-1">[1]</a></sup> nicknamed "<b>The Hoff</b>",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-2"><a href="#cite_note-2">[2]</a></sup> is an American actor, singer, producer, and businessman, who set a <a href="/wiki/Guinness_World_Records" title="Guinness World Records">Guinness World Record</a> as the most watched man on TV.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-3"><a href="#cite_note-3">[3]</a></sup> He first gained recognition on <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Young_and_The_Restless" title="The Young and The Restless">The Young and The Restless</a></i>, playing Dr. <a href="/wiki/Snapper_Foster" title="Snapper Foster">Snapper Foster</a>. His career continued with his leading role as <a href="/wiki/Michael_Knight_(Knight_Rider)" title="Michael Knight (Knight Rider)">Michael Knight</a> on <i><a href="/wiki/Knight_Rider_(1982_TV_series)" title="Knight Rider (1982 TV series)">Knight Rider</a></i> and as L.A. County Lifeguard <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Buchannon" title="Mitch Buchannon">Mitch Buchannon</a> in the series <i><a href="/wiki/Baywatch" title="Baywatch">Baywatch</a></i>. Hasselhoff produced <i>Baywatch</i> from the 1990s until 2001, when the series ended with <i><a href="/wiki/Baywatch" title="Baywatch">Baywatch Hawaii</a></i>. On screen, he appeared in films including <a href="/wiki/Click_(2006_film)" title="Click (2006 film)"><i>Click</i></a>, <i><a href="/wiki/DodgeBall:_A_True_Underdog_Story" title="DodgeBall: A True Underdog Story">Dodgeball</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie" title="The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie">The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/Hop_(film)" title="Hop (film)">Hop</a></i>.</p>
<p>In 2000, he made his Broadway debut in the musical <i><a href="/wiki/Jekyll_%26_Hyde_(musical)" title="Jekyll &amp; Hyde (musical)">Jekyll &amp; Hyde</a></i>. Following his debut he starred in other musicals including <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_(musical)" title="Chicago (musical)">Chicago</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Producers_(musical)" title="The Producers (musical)">The Producers</a></i>.</p>
<p></p>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_life">Early life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Early life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hasselhoff was born in <a href="/wiki/Baltimore" title="Baltimore">Baltimore, Maryland</a>, the son of Dolores Therese (née Mullinex/Mullinix; died February 11, 2009), a homemaker, and Joseph Vincent Hasselhoff, a business executive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-filmref_1-1"><a href="#cite_note-filmref-1">[1]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bookref1_4-0"><a href="#cite_note-bookref1-4">[4]</a></sup> His family is Roman Catholic, of German, Irish and English descent.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-bookref1_4-1"><a href="#cite_note-bookref1-4">[4]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-5"><a href="#cite_note-5">[5]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-6"><a href="#cite_note-6">[6]</a></sup> His great-great-grandmother, Meta, emigrated with her family to Baltimore from <a class="new" href="/w/index.php?title=V%C3%B6lkersen&amp;action=edit&amp;redlink=1" title="Völkersen (page does not exist)">Völkersen</a>, Germany, 30 kilometres (19 mi) from <a href="/wiki/Bremen" title="Bremen">Bremen</a>, in 1865.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-7"><a href="#cite_note-7">[7]</a></sup></p>
<p>He spent his pre-teen years in <a href="/wiki/Jacksonville,_Florida" title="Jacksonville, Florida">Jacksonville, Florida</a>, and later lived in <a href="/wiki/Atlanta" title="Atlanta">Atlanta</a>, <a href="/wiki/Georgia_(U.S._state)" title="Georgia (U.S. state)">Georgia</a>, where he attended <a href="/wiki/Marist_School_(Georgia)" title="Marist School (Georgia)">Marist High School</a>. Hasselhoff made his theatrical debut at age seven in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Peter_Pan_(musical)" title="Peter Pan (musical)">Peter Pan</a>, and ever since his childhood dream was to have a career on <a href="/wiki/Broadway_(Manhattan)" title="Broadway (Manhattan)">Broadway</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-8"><a href="#cite_note-8">[8]</a></sup> He graduated from <a href="/wiki/Lyons_Township_High_School" title="Lyons Township High School">Lyons Township High School</a> in <a href="/wiki/La_Grange,_Illinois" title="La Grange, Illinois">La Grange, Illinois</a> in 1970. He was a member of the speech team, senior discussion leaders, president of the choir, captain of the volleyball team and held roles in several plays (including one lead role as Matt in <i><a href="/wiki/The_Fantasticks" title="The Fantasticks">The Fantasticks</a></i>). He studied at <a href="/wiki/Oakland_University" title="Oakland University">Oakland University</a> before graduating with a degree in theater at the <a href="/wiki/California_Institute_of_the_Arts" title="California Institute of the Arts">California Institute of the Arts</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-9"><a href="#cite_note-9">[9]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Early_career">Early career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Early career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

</div>
</div>
<p>Hasselhoff portrayed Dr. "<a href="/wiki/Snapper_Foster" title="Snapper Foster">Snapper Foster</a>" on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Young_and_the_Restless" title="The Young and the Restless">The Young and the Restless</a></i> from 1975–82, leaving the series as the show wrote out many of their original characters. In 1979, he played "Simon" in <i><a href="/wiki/Starcrash" title="Starcrash">Starcrash</a></i>. He launched his singing career with guest appearances on the first season of children's program <i><a href="/wiki/Kids_Incorporated" title="Kids Incorporated">Kids Incorporated</a></i>, performing "Do You Love Me". He guest starred on two episodes of <i><a href="/wiki/Diff%27rent_Strokes" title="Diff'rent Strokes">Diff'rent Strokes</a></i> and the soap opera <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Santa_Barbara_(soap_opera)" title="Santa Barbara (soap opera)">Santa Barbara</a></i> as himself in 1984.</p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Knight_Rider"><i>Knight Rider</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Knight Rider">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hasselhoff was recruited by then <a href="/wiki/NBCUniversal_Television_Group" title="NBCUniversal Television Group">NBC</a> President <a href="/wiki/Brandon_Tartikoff" title="Brandon Tartikoff">Brandon Tartikoff</a> to star in the science-fiction series <i><a href="/wiki/Knight_Rider_(1982_TV_series)" title="Knight Rider (1982 TV series)">Knight Rider</a></i> from 1982 to 1986 as <a href="/wiki/Michael_Knight_(Knight_Rider)" title="Michael Knight (Knight Rider)">Michael Knight</a>. He has described <i>Knight Rider</i> as more than a TV show: "It's a phenomenon. It's bigger than <i><a href="/wiki/Baywatch" title="Baywatch">Baywatch</a></i> ever was." On the success of <i>Knight Rider</i> – "It's because it was about saving lives, not taking lives, and it was how one man really can make a difference. And we had a blast making it, and we made sure nobody died on the show; [just as] we made sure nobody ever drowned on <i>Baywatch</i>". (However, in the 1982 two-hour pilot "Knight Of The Phoenix", Muntzy is shot and killed in the parking lot. Also a female character died in the "Nobody Does It Better" episode, and a gang member was killed by Michael Knight in the "Short Notice" episode.)<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>He describes the acting he has done as "a little more difficult than if you had a regularly well-written script – like, if I was going to be in, say, <i><a href="/wiki/Reservoir_Dogs" title="Reservoir Dogs">Reservoir Dogs</a></i>, or <i><a href="/wiki/The_Godfather" title="The Godfather">The Godfather</a></i>, or <i><a href="/wiki/Dances_with_Wolves" title="Dances with Wolves">Dances with Wolves</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/Lawrence_of_Arabia_(film)" title="Lawrence of Arabia (film)">Lawrence of Arabia</a></i> or <i><a href="/wiki/ER_(TV_series)" title="ER (TV series)">ER</a></i>, I had to talk to a car."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-10"><a href="#cite_note-10">[10]</a></sup> His role in the show led him to a <a href="/wiki/People%27s_Choice_Awards" title="People's Choice Awards">People's Choice Award</a> for 'Most Popular Actor'.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-11"><a href="#cite_note-11">[11]</a></sup> Now, over 33 years later, the show is still playing throughout the world.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-12"><a href="#cite_note-12">[12]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="German.2FAustrian_popularity">German/Austrian popularity</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: German/Austrian popularity">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>While his star status waxed and waned in the USA, his popularity endured longer in Germany to the end of the 1980s. In 1989, David trained with <a href="/wiki/Patsy_Swayze" title="Patsy Swayze">Patsy Swayze</a> at <a href="/wiki/Debbie_Reynolds" title="Debbie Reynolds">Debbie Reynolds</a>' Studio in North Hollywood for the Austrian segment of his Knight Rider tour.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Baywatch"><i>Baywatch</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Baywatch">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hasselhoff returned to television on <i><a href="/wiki/Baywatch" title="Baywatch">Baywatch</a></i> which premiered in 1989. Although it was canceled after only one season, he believed the series had potential, so Hasselhoff revived it for the first-run syndication market in 1991, investing his own money and additionally functioning as executive producer. His contract stipulated royalties to be paid to him from the rerun profits, which gave him the financial liberty to buy back the rights to <i>Baywatch</i> from <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>.</p>
<p>In its second incarnation, <i>Baywatch</i> was much more successful. It ran for a total of 11 years and, from the 1990s until its series finale in 2001, was watched by almost 1 billion viewers across 140 countries, solidifying his status among the world's foremost television personalities of the said period.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13">[13]</a></sup> This success combined with his royalties and his other ventures have placed Hasselhoff's fortune at more than $100 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-14"><a href="#cite_note-14">[14]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 1991, Hasselhoff reprised his role as Michael Knight in the television film <i><a href="/wiki/Knight_Rider_2000" title="Knight Rider 2000">Knight Rider 2000</a></i> as a <a href="/wiki/Sequel" title="Sequel">sequel</a> to the original series. The movie served as a pilot for a proposed new series, but despite high ratings, the plan was abandoned.</p>
<p>In 1996, Hasselhoff was given a star on the <a href="/wiki/Hollywood_Walk_of_Fame" title="Hollywood Walk of Fame">Hollywood Walk of Fame</a>. In 1997, he performed a duet with Filipino singer <a href="/wiki/Regine_Velasquez" title="Regine Velasquez">Regine Velasquez</a>, which was used as the main theme for his 1998 movie <i>Legacy</i>. He made his Broadway debut in 2000 in the title role of <i><a href="/wiki/Jekyll_%26_Hyde_(musical)" title="Jekyll &amp; Hyde (musical)">Jekyll &amp; Hyde</a></i>. In August 2001, he hosted an event at the Conga Room, in Los Angeles honoring the Latin rock band <a href="/wiki/Renegade_(band)" title="Renegade (band)">Renegade</a> for record sales in excess of 30 million units worldwide, taking the stage with the Latin rockers and singing in Spanish.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-15"><a href="#cite_note-15">[15]</a></sup> Beginning on July 16, 2004, he played the lead role in London performances of <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_(musical)" title="Chicago (musical)">Chicago</a></i> for three months.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16">[16]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hasselhoff has made several <a href="/wiki/Self-parody" title="Self-parody">self-parodic</a> appearances in movies. He had a major role in <i><a href="/wiki/The_SpongeBob_SquarePants_Movie" title="The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie">The SpongeBob SquarePants Movie</a></i>, released November 19, 2004, starring as himself (though resembling his bygone <i>Baywatch</i> character) and meeting <a href="/wiki/SpongeBob_SquarePants_(character)" title="SpongeBob SquarePants (character)">SpongeBob</a> and <a href="/wiki/Patrick_Star" title="Patrick Star">Patrick</a> (his full name is heard once in the movie; he is referred to as "Hasselhoff"). Hasselhoff also had another short appearance in the movie <i><a href="/wiki/DodgeBall:_A_True_Underdog_Story" title="DodgeBall: A True Underdog Story">DodgeBall: A True Underdog Story</a></i> as the <a href="/wiki/Dodgeball" title="Dodgeball">dodgeball</a> coach to the German national dodgeball team, Team Hasselhoff. Berating his team after being eliminated from a tournament, he shouts "Ihr seid alle <i>Schweine</i>!" (translated: "You are all <i>pigs</i>!", a common German insult) and smashes a photo of himself in his <i>Baywatch</i> attire. In 2004's <i><a href="/wiki/EuroTrip" title="EuroTrip">EuroTrip</a></i>, Hasselhoff appears in a washroom. In the 2006 <a href="/wiki/Adam_Sandler" title="Adam Sandler">Adam Sandler</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Click_(2006_film)" title="Click (2006 film)">Click</a></i> Hasselhoff portrays Sandler's despicable boss. Hasselhoff also appeares in an episode of <i><a href="/wiki/Wildboyz" title="Wildboyz">Wildboyz</a></i>. In 2007, he again played himself in the <a href="/wiki/Jamie_Kennedy" title="Jamie Kennedy">Jamie Kennedy</a> comedy <i><a href="/wiki/Kickin%27_It_Old_Skool" title="Kickin' It Old Skool">Kickin' It Old Skool</a></i>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In his music video for "<a href="/wiki/Jump_in_My_Car" title="Jump in My Car">Jump in My Car</a>", he engages in self-parody; this time parodying his performance as Michael Knight in <i><a href="/wiki/Knight_Rider_(1982_TV_series)" title="Knight Rider (1982 TV series)">Knight Rider</a></i>. The car in the video was a black <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Pontiac_Trans_Am" title="Pontiac Trans Am">Pontiac Trans Am</a> with a pulsing <a href="/wiki/Light-emitting_diode" title="Light-emitting diode">LED</a> and an interior nearly identical to that of the <a href="/wiki/KITT" title="KITT">KITT</a> car in the series. The video was shot in Sydney, Australia using a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Right-hand_drive" title="Right-hand drive">right-hand drive</a> KITT replica, including KITT's <a href="/wiki/Ejection_seat" title="Ejection seat">ejection seat</a> system.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17">[17]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:DavidHasselhoff_20050926.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="1880" data-file-width="1728" height="239" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/DavidHasselhoff_20050926.jpg/220px-DavidHasselhoff_20050926.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/DavidHasselhoff_20050926.jpg/330px-DavidHasselhoff_20050926.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b9/DavidHasselhoff_20050926.jpg/440px-DavidHasselhoff_20050926.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>

<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:DavidHasselhoff_20050926.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hasselhoff in 2005</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In November 2006, <a href="/wiki/Mel_Brooks" title="Mel Brooks">Mel Brooks</a> announced Hasselhoff would portray Roger DeBris, the director of the <a href="/wiki/Nazism" title="Nazism">Nazi</a> musical <i><a href="/wiki/The_Producers_(1968_film)" title="The Producers (1968 film)">Springtime for Hitler</a></i>, in the <a href="/wiki/Las_Vegas_Valley" title="Las Vegas Valley">Las Vegas</a> production of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Producers_(musical)" title="The Producers (musical)">The Producers</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18">[18]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2006, Hasselhoff, became a co-judge on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Got_Talent" title="America's Got Talent">America's Got Talent</a></i>, a show that showcases America's best amateur entertainers. He also judged in the second, third and fourth seasons alongside <a href="/wiki/Sharon_Osbourne" title="Sharon Osbourne">Sharon Osbourne</a> and <a href="/wiki/Piers_Morgan" title="Piers Morgan">Piers Morgan</a>. On the 2007 season finale, Hasselhoff sang "This is the Moment." He was replaced by comedian <a href="/wiki/Howie_Mandel" title="Howie Mandel">Howie Mandel</a> for season five.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19">[19]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_career">Later career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Later career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hasselhoff produced <i><a href="/wiki/Baywatch" title="Baywatch">Baywatch</a></i> for first run syndication. He has spoken at both the Oxford and Cambridge Student Unions.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20">[20]</a></sup></p>
<p>He was a celebrity cast member on the eleventh season of <i><a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Dancing with the Stars (U.S. TV series)">Dancing with the Stars</a></i> which increased in ratings by 36% from the previous year, and served as a judge on <a href="/wiki/NBC" title="NBC">NBC</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Got_Talent" title="America's Got Talent">America's Got Talent</a></i> from 2006-09. In 2011, he joined the <i><a href="/wiki/Britain%27s_Got_Talent" title="Britain's Got Talent">Britain's Got Talent</a></i> judging panel, replacing <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21">[21]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hasselhoff was later honored on <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">Comedy Central</a>'s <i>The <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central_Roast" title="Comedy Central Roast">Comedy Central Roast</a> of David Hasselhoff</i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-22"><a href="#cite_note-22">[22]</a></sup> in addition to receiving the International Star of the Year Award for Outstanding Contribution to Global Entertainment by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bollywood_Awards" title="Bollywood Awards">Bollywood Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23">[23]</a></sup> He was awarded the Comeback Star of the Year award during the <a href="/wiki/VH1_Big_in_%2706_Awards" title="VH1 Big in '06 Awards">VH1 Big in '06 Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-24"><a href="#cite_note-24">[24]</a></sup></p>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:David_Hasselhoff1.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2592" data-file-width="3872" height="147" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/David_Hasselhoff1.jpg/220px-David_Hasselhoff1.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/David_Hasselhoff1.jpg/330px-David_Hasselhoff1.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/2/21/David_Hasselhoff1.jpg/440px-David_Hasselhoff1.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:David_Hasselhoff1.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
David Hasselhoff waving the checkered flag at the 2008 <a href="/wiki/Gumball_3000" title="Gumball 3000">Gumball 3000</a></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In 2008, Hasselhoff was a featured guest in a <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen" title="Volkswagen">Volkswagen</a> commercial, where he talked about the company selling more cars in Europe and the rest of the world than any other brand. In response, the black <a href="/wiki/Volkswagen_Beetle" title="Volkswagen Beetle">Beetle</a> commented that Hasselhoff is "not so big" in Brazil. In late October of that same year, Hasselhoff played a bit part in the EA real time strategy video game <i><a href="/wiki/Command_%26_Conquer:_Red_Alert_3" title="Command &amp; Conquer: Red Alert 3">Command &amp; Conquer: Red Alert 3</a></i> as vice president of the United States, while starring in its promotional microsite, conquerthislife.com, which featured several tongue-in-cheek videos as well as a Hasselhoff soundboard.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>In February 2008, towards the end of the <i><a href="/wiki/Knight_Rider_(2008_film)" title="Knight Rider (2008 film)">Knight Rider 2008</a></i>, he reprised his career-making role as Michael Knight as he walked on to introduce himself to his on-screen son, Mike Traceur. On November 12, 2008, he became the first celebrity downloadable character for the <a href="/wiki/PlayStation_Network" title="PlayStation Network">PlayStation Network</a>'s video game <i><a href="/wiki/Pain_(video_game)" title="Pain (video game)">Pain</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25">[25]</a></sup></p>
<p>In September 2009, he featured on a radio podcast for <a href="/wiki/Compare_the_Meerkat" title="Compare the Meerkat">Compare the Meerkat</a>, part of the advertising for British website, <a href="/wiki/Comparethemarket.com" title="Comparethemarket.com">Comparethemarket.com</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-26"><a href="#cite_note-26">[26]</a></sup> He was the subject of an <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Early_Day_Motion" title="Early Day Motion">Early Day Motion</a> in the <a href="/wiki/House_of_Commons_of_the_United_Kingdom" title="House of Commons of the United Kingdom">House of Commons of the United Kingdom</a> as a result of his support for the re-opening of <a href="/wiki/Morecambe_Winter_Gardens" title="Morecambe Winter Gardens">Morecambe Winter Gardens</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27">[27]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2010, Hasselhoff guest hosted professional wrestling's <i><a href="/wiki/WWE_Raw" title="WWE Raw">WWE Raw</a></i> in London, England. On August 15, 2010, <a href="/wiki/Comedy_Central" title="Comedy Central">Comedy Central</a> aired a special "<a href="/wiki/Roast_(comedy)" title="Roast (comedy)">roast</a>" of Hasselhoff.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-28"><a href="#cite_note-28">[28]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hasselhoff returned to <i>The Young and the Restless</i>, reprising his role as "Snapper" for a short arc that aired in mid-June 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29">[29]</a></sup> Hasselhoff appeared as a contestant on <a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._season_11)" title="Dancing with the Stars (U.S. season 11)">season 11</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/Dancing_with_the_Stars_(U.S._TV_series)" title="Dancing with the Stars (U.S. TV series)">Dancing with the Stars</a></i>. His professional dance partner was <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Kym_Johnson" title="Kym Johnson">Kym Johnson</a>. On September 21, 2010, they were the first couple eliminated from the competition. Coincidentally, Hasselhoff competed against <a href="/wiki/Brandy_Norwood" title="Brandy Norwood">Brandy Norwood</a>, who judged alongside him in the <a href="/wiki/America%27s_Got_Talent_(season_1)" title="America's Got Talent (season 1)">first season</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/America%27s_Got_Talent" title="America's Got Talent">America's Got Talent</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30">[30]</a></sup></p>
<p>In October 2010, it was announced that he would be playing Captain Hook in the New Wimbledon Theatre production of the pantomime "Peter Pan" from December 2010 to January 2011.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-31"><a href="#cite_note-31">[31]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32">[32]</a></sup> He has reprised his role of "Hoff the Hook"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-33"><a href="#cite_note-33">[33]</a></sup> for 2012 at the <a href="/wiki/Manchester_Opera_House" title="Manchester Opera House">Opera House</a>, <a href="/wiki/Manchester" title="Manchester">Manchester</a>.</p>
<p>In 2011, he was a guest judge at the Belgian Idols competition.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-34"><a href="#cite_note-34">[34]</a></sup> Hasselhoff became a judge on <i><a href="/wiki/Britain%27s_Got_Talent" title="Britain's Got Talent">Britain's Got Talent</a></i> in 2011 alongside <a href="/wiki/Amanda_Holden" title="Amanda Holden">Amanda Holden</a>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_McIntyre" title="Michael McIntyre">Michael McIntyre</a> and <a href="/wiki/Simon_Cowell" title="Simon Cowell">Simon Cowell</a>. However, Hasselhoff was axed after only one series on the show.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-35"><a href="#cite_note-35">[35]</a></sup> In 2011, he revived his music career with a short tour across <a href="/wiki/Germany" title="Germany">Germany</a>, <a href="/wiki/Austria" title="Austria">Austria</a> and <a href="/wiki/Switzerland" title="Switzerland">Switzerland</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-36"><a href="#cite_note-36">[36]</a></sup> In the same year, Hasselhoff is featured in the trailer of the spin-off downloadable game, <i><a href="/wiki/Burnout_Crash!" title="Burnout Crash!">Burnout Crash!</a></i>. On October 1, 2011, David Hasselhoff attended Knightcon 2011 at Xscape, Castleford, UK, with girlfriend Hayley Roberts. The event was also attended by former Knight Rider cohorts Rebecca Holden (April Curtis in Season 2), Peter Parros (Reginald Cornilius III (RC3) in Season 4), and Michael Scheffe, the designer of KITT.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2013)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> In 2012, he was a contestant on <i><a href="/wiki/The_Celebrity_Apprentice_Australia_(season_2)" title="The Celebrity Apprentice Australia (season 2)">The Celebrity Apprentice Australia</a></i> . He appeared on '8 out of 10 Cats' on May 11, 2012, and entertained the audience by using the word 'willy'.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<p>On February 24, 2014 he opened his own 10-week talk show in Sweden on <a href="/wiki/TV3_(Sweden)" title="TV3 (Sweden)">TV3</a>, in English.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-37"><a href="#cite_note-37">[37]</a></sup> A similar show was later recorded in <a href="/wiki/Finland" title="Finland">Finland</a>, premiering on <a href="/wiki/Sub_(TV_channel)" title="Sub (TV channel)">Sub</a> on April 2, 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-38"><a href="#cite_note-38">[38]</a></sup></p>
<p>On <a href="/wiki/New_Year%27s_Eve#Germany" title="New Year's Eve">New Year's Eve</a> he performed again at the <a href="/wiki/Brandenburg_Gate" title="Brandenburg Gate">Brandenburg Gate</a>, arriving late because his plane was diverted to Hannover.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-nbcTor_39-0"><a href="#cite_note-nbcTor-39">[39]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Tages_40-0"><a href="#cite_note-Tages-40">[40]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-41"><a href="#cite_note-41">[41]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hasselhoff had a major role in <i><a href="/wiki/Sharknado_3:_Oh_Hell_No!" title="Sharknado 3: Oh Hell No!">Sharknado 3: Oh Hell No!</a></i> which premiered globally on July 22, 2015. He then starred in a new musical, <i>Last Night a DJ Saved My Life</i> at the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Blackpool_Opera_House" title="Blackpool Opera House">Blackpool Opera House</a>, late in 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-42"><a href="#cite_note-42">[42]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Get_Hasselhoff_to_Number_1_campaign">Get Hasselhoff to Number 1 campaign</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Get Hasselhoff to Number 1 campaign">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On April 21, 2006, fans of David Hasselhoff launched a tongue-in-cheek website "Get Hasselhoff to Number 1"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-43"><a href="#cite_note-43">[43]</a></sup> in an attempt to get the 1989 hit "Looking for Freedom" to the top of the UK music charts through Internet downloads of the single. The campaign attracted attention on British radio and television broadcasts, in the national press<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-44"><a href="#cite_note-44">[44]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-45"><a href="#cite_note-45">[45]</a></sup> and on the Internet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-46"><a href="#cite_note-46">[46]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-47"><a href="#cite_note-47">[47]</a></sup> Over 40,000 people signed up to receive the "Hoff Alert" e-mail when the time had come to purchase the single. The focus of the campaign shifted to "<a href="/wiki/Jump_in_My_Car" title="Jump in My Car">Jump in My Car</a>", when that was actually released as a single, and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a> DJ <a href="/wiki/Scott_Mills" title="Scott Mills">Scott Mills</a> lent his support.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-48"><a href="#cite_note-48">[48]</a></sup> On October 3, 2006, "the Hoff Alert" was sent out, and Hasselhoff promptly gained his highest ever UK chart entry (number 3) on October 8, 2006.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (July 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="HoffSpace">HoffSpace</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: HoffSpace">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Irina_Slutsky_with_David_Hasselhoff.jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="453" data-file-width="604" height="165" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Irina_Slutsky_with_David_Hasselhoff.jpg/220px-Irina_Slutsky_with_David_Hasselhoff.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Irina_Slutsky_with_David_Hasselhoff.jpg/330px-Irina_Slutsky_with_David_Hasselhoff.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/b/b1/Irina_Slutsky_with_David_Hasselhoff.jpg/440px-Irina_Slutsky_with_David_Hasselhoff.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Irina_Slutsky_with_David_Hasselhoff.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Hasselhoff with journalist <a href="/wiki/Irina_Slutsky" title="Irina Slutsky">Irina Slutsky</a> promoting social networking venture HoffSpace</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Hasselhoff has launched a MySpace-like <a href="/wiki/Social_networking_service" title="Social networking service">social networking site</a>, known as "HoffSpace."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-49"><a href="#cite_note-49">[49]</a></sup> He did so in part as a response to people opening false social-networking pages in his name,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-50"><a href="#cite_note-50">[50]</a></sup> as well as those of his children.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-51"><a href="#cite_note-51">[51]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="The_Hasselhoffs"><i>The Hasselhoffs</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: The Hasselhoffs">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hasselhoff and his daughters, Taylor-Ann and <a href="/wiki/Hayley_Hasselhoff" title="Hayley Hasselhoff">Hayley</a>, starred in a reality series on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/A%26E_(TV_channel)" title="A&amp;E (TV channel)">A&amp;E</a> called <i>The Hasselhoffs</i>. The series launched on Sunday, December 5, 2010, and focused on Hasselhoff's attempts to resuscitate his career and launch his daughters onto the Hollywood stage.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-aeshow1_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-aeshow1-52">[52]</a></sup></p>
<p>On Friday, December 10, 2010, A&amp;E confirmed in a statement that, after airing just two episodes, <i>The Hasselhoffs</i> had been canceled. According to Nielsen Co. ratings, the first episode was seen by 718,000 viewers. Viewers dropped to 505,000 for the second installment, which aired on the same evening. The full series aired in the UK on May 30, 2011 on <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Bio._(UK)" title="Bio. (UK)">The Biography Channel</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53">[53]</a></sup></p>
<p>Hasselhoff stars in a casino-style game series online, produced in partnership with <a href="/wiki/Eric_Bischoff" title="Eric Bischoff">Eric Bischoff</a><sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (February 2014)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup> with Europe being among the first markets to roll out the game. In keeping with internet and online gambling culture in the UK, "The Hoff" series of games includes video slots and scratch-card type games, all played for real money in Europe's online casino environment. The first in the series of games launched on Valentine's Day in early March, 2013, with media and promotional activities commencing in early February.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-54"><a href="#cite_note-54">[54]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Hoff_the_Record"><i>Hoff the Record</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Hoff the Record">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote" role="note">Main article: <a href="/wiki/Hoff_the_Record" title="Hoff the Record">Hoff the Record</a></div>
<p>In 2014 UK channel <a href="/wiki/Dave_(TV_channel)" title="Dave (TV channel)">Dave</a> announced that it had commissioned <i>Hoff the Record</i>, a sitcom series in which Hasselhoff plays a fictionalized version of himself. The series started airing on 18 June 2015.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55">[55]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Music_career">Music career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Music career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Looking_for_freedom"><i>Looking for freedom</i></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Looking for freedom">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>His music career took off in the late 1980s and achieved success at the tops of the charts, with his album "<a href="/wiki/Looking_for_Freedom_(album)" title="Looking for Freedom (album)">Looking for freedom</a>" which went triple platinum in Europe. He had one #1 hit in the German pop charts in 1989 ("<a href="/wiki/Looking_for_Freedom_(song)" title="Looking for Freedom (song)">Looking for Freedom</a>").<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-GerHits_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-GerHits-56">[56]</a></sup> He was noted for his performance of the single at the <a href="/wiki/Berlin_Wall" title="Berlin Wall">Berlin Wall</a> on New Year's Eve 1989, days after the collapse of the wall. Wearing a piano-keyboard tie and a leather jacket covered in motion lights, Hasselhoff stood in a bucket crane and performed the song along with the crowd. The performance has had a lasting impact on <a href="/wiki/Culture_of_Germany" title="Culture of Germany">German pop-culture</a> with Hasselhoff commenting that the song became an "anthem" and "song of hope" for the people of <a href="/wiki/East_Germany" title="East Germany">East Germany</a>. In 2004, Hasselhoff lamented the lack of a photo of him in the <a href="/wiki/Checkpoint_Charlie_Museum" title="Checkpoint Charlie Museum">Checkpoint Charlie Museum</a> in Berlin.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-57"><a href="#cite_note-57">[57]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58">[58]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Later_music_career">Later music career</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Later music career">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In 1993, he released the single 'Pingu Dance' based on the popular children's show 'Pingu'. In 1994, he was scheduled to perform a concert on <a href="/wiki/Pay-per-view" title="Pay-per-view">pay-per-view</a> from Atlantic City. The concert was expected to help reignite his singing career in the United States. However, on the night of the concert, <a href="/wiki/O._J._Simpson" title="O. J. Simpson">O. J. Simpson</a> was involved in a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Slow-speed_chase" title="Slow-speed chase">police chase</a> in southern California. Viewership of the concert was significantly lower than expected due to the live coverage of the chase, and the event was ultimately a $1.5 million loss.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-59"><a href="#cite_note-59">[59]</a></sup></p>
<p>In May 2006, Hasselhoff returned to the spotlight after he was mentioned in an interview of <a href="/wiki/Dirk_Nowitzki" title="Dirk Nowitzki">Dirk Nowitzki</a>, an <a href="/wiki/National_Basketball_Association" title="National Basketball Association">NBA</a> star playing for the <a href="/wiki/Dallas_Mavericks" title="Dallas Mavericks">Dallas Mavericks</a> and a native of Germany. Nowitzki was asked what he does to concentrate when shooting foul shots. Dirk replied that he sings "Looking for Freedom" to himself. He meant this as a joke but it was thought to be a serious answer. Shortly thereafter, Hasselhoff attended the May 26, 2006, Mavericks home playoff game where they faced the <a href="/wiki/Phoenix_Suns" title="Phoenix Suns">Phoenix Suns</a> in the NBA Western Conference Finals. Interviewed by <a href="/wiki/Craig_Sager" title="Craig Sager">Craig Sager</a>, Hasselhoff stated he was as much a fan of Nowitzki as Nowitzki was a fan of him. In The <a href="/wiki/2006_NBA_Finals" title="2006 NBA Finals">2006 NBA Finals</a>, fans of the <a href="/wiki/Miami_Heat" title="Miami Heat">Miami Heat</a> in the <a href="/wiki/American_Airlines_Arena" title="American Airlines Arena">American Airlines Arena</a> held up facial photos of Hasselhoff and chanted his name when Nowitzki went to the foul line. On August 2, 2006, he proclaimed himself "King of the Internet" in a tongue-in-cheek advertisement for <a href="/wiki/TalkTalk_Business" title="TalkTalk Business">Pipex</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-60"><a href="#cite_note-60">[60]</a></sup></p>
<p>In December 2008, he sang the <a href="/wiki/National_anthem" title="National anthem">national anthem</a> at the <a href="/wiki/National_Collegiate_Athletic_Association" title="National Collegiate Athletic Association">NCAA</a> <a href="/wiki/2008_Las_Vegas_Bowl" title="2008 Las Vegas Bowl">Las Vegas Bowl</a>. Although the game was televised live by <a href="/wiki/ESPN" title="ESPN">ESPN</a>, the station chose not to broadcast Hasselhoff's performance.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61">[61]</a></sup></p>
<p>In 2015, he recorded the single "True Survivor", accompanied by a music video, which featured as the lead track for the 2015 Swedish short film <a href="/wiki/Kung_Fury" title="Kung Fury">Kung Fury</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62">[62]</a></sup> The song was composed by <a href="/wiki/Mitch_Murder" title="Mitch Murder">Mitch Murder</a> (Johan Bengtsson). Recorded in Sweden, the song and the video is designed as an ostentatious over-the-top 1980s homage/parody, with the video featuring dinosaurs, kung fu, <a href="/wiki/Adolf_Hitler" title="Adolf Hitler">Adolf Hitler</a>, skateboarding, Norse Gods and time travelling. Hasselhoff claimed that he had received the offer to record the song and the video by a request from Sweden Universal to "sing a tribute to the '80s".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-63"><a href="#cite_note-63">[63]</a></sup> Hasselhoff performed a live version of the song during the 2016 <a href="/wiki/Guldbagge_Awards" title="Guldbagge Awards">Guldbagge Awards</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-64"><a href="#cite_note-64">[64]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-65"><a href="#cite_note-65">[65]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Personal_life">Personal life</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Personal life">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Hasselhoff's autobiography <i>Making Waves</i> was released in the United Kingdom in September 2006. In an interview in April 2006, he promised the book would present the "last chapter" regarding controversial elements of his personal life.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-66"><a href="#cite_note-66">[66]</a></sup></p>
<p>Since 2013 Hasselhoff has dated Hayley Roberts, from the town of <a href="/wiki/Glynneath" title="Glynneath">Glynneath</a> in <a href="/wiki/Wales" title="Wales">Wales</a>. He is a fan of Welsh <a href="/wiki/Rugby_union" title="Rugby union">rugby union</a>, and they regularly attend rugby matches in Wales.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-67"><a href="#cite_note-67">[67]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68">[68]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-69"><a href="#cite_note-69">[69]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-70"><a href="#cite_note-70">[70]</a></sup></p>
<p>In November 2015, Hasselhoff posted a <a href="/wiki/YouTube" title="YouTube">YouTube</a> video in which he announced that he had changed his name to "David Hoff".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-71"><a href="#cite_note-71">[71]</a></sup> It was then reported that he was not changing his name; that the video was an excerpt from an upcoming advertising campaign.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-72"><a href="#cite_note-72">[72]</a></sup></p>
<p>After touring <a href="/wiki/Glasgow" title="Glasgow">Glasgow</a> during late 2015, Hasselhoff stated that he supports <a href="/wiki/Scottish_Professional_Football_League" title="Scottish Professional Football League">Scottish football</a> team <a href="/wiki/Partick_Thistle_F.C." title="Partick Thistle F.C.">Partick Thistle F.C.</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73">[73]</a></sup></p>
<p>He resides in <a href="/wiki/Southern_California" title="Southern California">Southern California</a> with his two daughters, five dogs, and other pets.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74">[74]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Family">Family</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Family">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Hasselhoff was married to actress <a href="/wiki/Catherine_Hickland" title="Catherine Hickland">Catherine Hickland</a> from March 24, 1984 to March 1, 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-filmref_1-2"><a href="#cite_note-filmref-1">[1]</a></sup> Their wedding was recreated in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/List_of_Knight_Rider_episodes_(season_4)" title="List of Knight Rider episodes (season 4)">the <i>Knight Rider</i> Season 4</a> episode "The Scent of Roses" which first aired on January 3, 1986.</p>
<p>Hasselhoff married actress <a href="/wiki/Pamela_Bach" title="Pamela Bach">Pamela Bach</a> in December 1989.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pamelabachdivorce_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-pamelabachdivorce-75">[75]</a></sup> The couple have two daughters: Taylor Ann Hasselhoff, born May 5, 1990,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76">[76]</a></sup> who attended the <a href="/wiki/University_of_Arizona" title="University of Arizona">University of Arizona</a> and was cast for the 2015 season of <i><a href="/wiki/Rich_Kids_of_Beverly_Hills" title="Rich Kids of Beverly Hills">Rich Kids of Beverly Hills</a></i>, and actress <a href="/wiki/Hayley_Hasselhoff" title="Hayley Hasselhoff">Hayley Hasselhoff</a>, born August 28, 1992.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77">[77]</a></sup> In January 2006, Hasselhoff announced he was filing for divorce, citing irreconcilable differences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pamelabachdivorce_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-pamelabachdivorce-75">[75]</a></sup> Their divorce was finalized in August, 2006.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ex-attorney_78-0"><a href="#cite_note-ex-attorney-78">[78]</a></sup> Bach was given custody of one daughter and Hasselhoff custody of the other,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79">[79]</a></sup> until Hasselhoff later obtained custody of both.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-ex-attorney_78-1"><a href="#cite_note-ex-attorney-78">[78]</a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Alcoholism">Alcoholism</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Alcoholism">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>On May 3, 2007, a home video surfaced of Hasselhoff apparently in an alcoholic stupor. His daughter, Taylor Ann, who shot the video, can be heard saying, "Tell me you are going to stop, tell me you are going to stop." The daughter also warns her father he could be jeopardizing his spot on the Las Vegas production of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Producers_(musical)" title="The Producers (musical)">The Producers</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80">[80]</a></sup> In the wake of the leaked clip, Hasselhoff issued a statement saying it was recorded by Taylor Ann so that he could see how he behaved while intoxicated and the footage was deliberately released.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81">[81]</a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-82"><a href="#cite_note-82">[82]</a></sup> As a result of the video, Hasselhoff's visitation rights with his two daughters were suspended on May 7, 2007, for two weeks until the video's authenticity and distributor were determined.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83">[83]</a></sup> In May 2009, Hasselhoff's attorney, Mel Goldsman, described Hasselhoff as "a recovering alcoholic".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84">[84]</a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Filmography">Filmography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Filmography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Honors_and_awards">Honors and awards</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=David_Hasselhoff&amp;action=edit&amp;section=28" title="Edit section: Honors and awards">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<ul>
<li>1983 – Favorite Male Performer in a New TV Program: People's Choice Awards</li>
<li>2005 – International Star of the Year Award for Outstanding Contribution to Global Entertainment: Bollywood Awards</li>
<li>2006 – Comeback Star of the Year: VH1 Big in '06 Awards</li>
<li>2010 – The Comedy Central Roast of David Hasselhoff: Comedy Central</li>
</ul>
